< text>
I recently bought a tux here and had the tailoring done when I bought it because I was in a hurry. Normally I get my tailoring done at a small independent shop where I have been going for years, but I just didn't have the time to make it happen on that occasion.
The tailoring here was a little expensive but otherwise very good quality. I figured that the premium price was worth the convenience of this shop being near my house and recently brought in a few pieces that needed some adjustments, only to find out that they "don't do outside tailoring" (i.e. they won't work on pieces that you haven't bought directly from them). Seems pretty class-less and short-sighted. Won't be shopping here again.<//text>

<Review>Over the past two days I've received thousands of emails asking if the pretzel crust at LC is worth a try. Not to worry fans- I have heard your voice and have an answer to your questions.

YES. The crust would make even Snyder's of Hanover proud. The pizza is solid, and further enhanced by the fact it costs $6 and is ready in as many minutes.

What I would NOT recommend are the chicken wings. If you a really curious as to what they taste/feel like, take a bite out of a microwaved sponge soaked in barbeque sauce. The only earthly substance squishier and slimier than the "meat" is the fleshy tissue (presumably an attempt to emulate skin?) that it is wrapped in. Perhaps the most concerning part is that the bucket of sloppy meat products they are passing off as wings cost more than the pizza.

Ultimately, however, I think the blame falls on me. Shame on me for ordering $8 wings from LC. Since I should have known better, they still get 4 stars.<//Review>< pictures>

<Date>1551863774183< /Date>< Review>
Fam, I've done Lil C's, and this ain't it. I know, we've all eaten sweaty cardboard and passed it off as pizza. You know what, sometimes it reminds you of the pioneers, alright?

That being said, this is the slowest and toughest Little Caesars to ever return to. I've tried 4 times, and that's 3 times too many. I've seen a Hot N' Ready sitting in the warming box, just waiting to be scarfed down. I paid the nice cashier fella my $5+Tax. He says, "Ok, just a minute." The next thing I know, he's disappeared to the back, and then comes back staring at a stack of receipts. I mean lots of receipts. You'd have thought he was translating papyrus.

I look at my watch. Horror. Shock. That same pizza is sitting in the warmer, 5 more people have come in and ordered, and the poor chap is still running around with those RECEIPTS. At this point, there's a cacophony of conversations, videos being played on phones, and disgruntled coughs and mutters.

The watch is pulling at me...look down, I must. It's been almost 15 minutes and I still see that pizza sitting in the warmer. Finally, for a reason unknown to me, the pizza is pulled out and shakily handed my way. "Need anything else sir?"
Nothing you can give me.
Some self-respect maybe. More self-control. A different choice of Little Caesar's. I'm not even sure anymore.

I crack open that box once I get to the car. I peel a slice from its comrades, and I'm met with another disappointment.
The slice is stiff as a board.

Save yourselves, go elsewhere.</Review>

Of course meals were delicious here. Really good pesto pasta with chicken, fish and chips. Unlimited salad and soup for each meal ordered. Restaurant times are limited and can get full quickly. Try to get there when they open for dinner at 5:30pm. Way way way way pricey. This lodge should a few affordable food places built cafeteria style to accommodate large numbers of tourists instead of a fancy pricey restaurant in the middle of nowhere. Other places to eat are more than 30 min drive from here. So bring meals and snack with you or be prepared to drive far distance for each meal or pay insane amounts at river restaurant.<//text>

Shannon Meadows< /username>
< Date>
1562532418492<//Date>
<Rate>3</Rate>< text>
They're one of two restaurants just outside Yosemite, so this venue could really be so much more. It has a great start: it sits on the bank of the Merced River and the view is wonderful. The staff is friendly and we get the 'cabin' theme, but the interior is dated and dank, it smells stale, the carpet is worn, and it just feels pieced together. For that reason, we're happy we requested to sit on the deck outside overlooking the river. Our server, Shawn, was personable and answered our questions about items the menu. My pesto fettuccine was tasty, but nothing extraordinary. Still I was satisfied, and enjoyed a nice Chardonnay with it. My husband's chicken Marsala was 'nothing special,' although the mashed potatoes were good. He was pretty disappointed with what he ordered. The meals came with a salad bar (which may explain the higher cost for entrees other reviewers talked about), but it was the least appealing of everything we experienced there. The bar itself was located in a small, poorly-lit, room that seemed like an afterthought. The lettuce/spring mix didn't appear fresh and the serving spoons and trays looked like they hadn't been wiped down for several hours. The salad bar was average. The one upside is that the vegetable soup tasted fresh and it was delicious. Overall, our experience there was only average, quite unremarkable. We highly recommend the pizzeria next door, though. We assume they're owned by the same group, but are not sure. Looking back, we'd have rather eaten pizza two nights in a row because it was that good and our experience at River Restaurant was just okay.< /text>

< Pictures>
[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNZqv8Q10WyMbFUJOBfsV_Q6XUvFyYul9xiSPQG=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /Pictures>

1525229508388<//Time>
< review>
The restaurant isn't always open in convenient hours, especially in winter, but when open, stays fairly busy. It appears fairly clean in the dining area. They have an adequate soup and salad bar. The menu is not extensive, but usually I can find something I can select from. While I consider the food fairly mediocre, I realize we do not have a world class chef from New York or Paris. We are in a little drink water town...wait we're not actually "in" a town, we're at a hotel, so we have a cook who lives in the back woods and we wonder why we don't get haute cuisine? Personally, I'd be happy with a really good chuck wagon cook--we didn't even get that, so I give only 3 stars. SECOND. I wish people would stop complaining about how much everything costs. Think just a minute will you. Where did the food come from? Out there grown on those rocks? No, it was trucked in in trucks at a high cost of gasoline as everyone well knows. Then tack on that the labor of loading and that of the driver to get the food here. I have driven behind some of these trucks going 10-15 miles per hour up the long hills. IT TAKES FOREVER! How much do you think that costs? Wait. We haven't gotten the food to the restaurant yet. Get it here and pay to get it unloaded. Refrigerate it (oh yes, higher electricity bills because the power lines are far more expensive to place, here.). Now, clean and pay the overpaid cook to waste what shouldn't be wasted and cook the meal, cook the wrong meal, recook the meal, and lose the tips for everyone because of complaints about the slowness and poor quality of the meal.Costs rack up in a variety of ways. Just remember, though, everything is expensive up here because it ALL has to be trucked up here--hence, the higher prices and fewer choices. Complain about the cooking, yes, but be aware of the why of higher prices.</review>

< Text>
Short version: Basically a no-call, no-show for my maintenance/service appointment.  I called 30 mins after my appt time window (2-6pm) closed and was told I could wait another hour and maybe someone would come by, or I could re-schedule.. no one called me ahead of time to let me know what was going on.  If someone would have called and given me a heads-up in a timely fashion, this would not have been a big deal, I would have been OK w a re-schedule.. but to wait around the house for hours and not get one was upsetting.

I was quite hopeful of a good experience with this company as the initial communication was great - confirmation email and text, and the same for notifications when the actual appointment time came.  The earliest appointment was over a week for away from my initial call, but this was just for annual maintenance, so no big deal there.

On the day of my appointment, I call and leave a voicemail at the office letting them know that I will be around and available earlier in the day if that works vs the later 2-6 pm appointment time.  I get a call back 30 minutes later and they leave a VM stating that they are booked up and they "guarantee my appointment between 4 and 6 pm" (their words).

I busy myself around the house until 630 pm and give the office a call again.  The woman I speak to states the technician is still at the first place he went to this afternoon, but should be done sometime soon.. they have been slammed since a heatwave a week or two ago.  And it is a Saturday, so they only have one technician on.

I ask why no one called me to let me know that my "guaranteed" appointment time would not be kept.. there is only one technician to keep track of..  No good answer provided.

She asks me if I want to just wait for another hour or so to see if the tech can come by then.  I decline and say please just cancel my appointment.  She is apparently surprised by this answer and then states something to the effect of: oh good, the technician can go by someone's house w a broken AC then.. apparently oblivious to the fact that I am quite dissatisfied with this whole experience and wasting my afternoon waiting around for someone that never showed up and didn't bother to even call.

Perhaps this is just an isolated incident, but if there are other stories like mine up here on Yelp/Google, then maybe try someone else for your HVAC needs.  Another tip that I wish I was told earlier, is that they only have 1 technician on weekends - you may have better luck on weekdays?</Text>
